SUBJECT:
124 Warren Road (Permit# WC-2024-000243) Resident Appeals - Statement of Decision
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Statement of Decision denying the appeals for a wireless permit application that was approved by the Director of 
Public Works under the City's 2021 Wireless Ordinance and Design Standards for a wireless facility at 124 Warren Road 
(Wireless Permit # WC-2024-000243)
BACKGROUND:
On February 12, 2025, the Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission (”Commission”) held an appeal relating to the 
Public Works Director's approval of the Wireless Permit # WC-2024-000243 at 124 Warren Road. The Director’s Decision 
was issued on January 17, 2025 pursuant to the City’s 2021 Wireless Ordinance and Design Standards. The Commission 
denied the appeals by a 5-0 vote. The written statement explaining the legal and factual basis for the Commission’s 
decision is included with this report as Attachment 1.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The public hearing to consider resident appeals does not have a direct impact on the City’s Budget other than costs 
associated with staff time which are paid for by the permit applicant.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This item is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a physical change in 
the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 - Statement of Decision
STAFF CONTACT
Jason Hallare, Senior Engineer
jhallare@cityofsanmateo.org

Statement of Decision by the San Mateo Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission in the Matter of an 
Appeal of the Public Works Director’s Decision to Grant a Wireless Permit
(124 Warren Road, Permit # WC-2024-000243)
Section 1. Introduction
San Mateo Municipal Code (SMMC) Chapter 17.10 establishes reasonable, uniform and comprehensive 
standards and procedures for wireless facilities deployment, construction, installation, collocation, modification, 
operation, relocation, and removal within the City's public right-of-way, consistent with and to the extent 
permitted under federal and California state law (“Ordinance”).  To that end, SMMC Section 17.10.040 requires 
a wireless permit, City of San Mateo (“City”) pole license (if the proposed facility is located on a City owed pole), 
various other permits and approvals, and fees to be submitted prior to the installation of any proposed wireless 
facility.
SMMC Section 17.10.070(a)-(b) specifies the Public Works Director (“Director”), or designee, shall approve, 
conditionally approve, or deny an application for a wireless permit upon a finding that: 
(1) the applicant and the proposed wireless facility complies with all the requirements of SMMC Chapter 
17.10, and the design standards and application requirements in effect at the time of application; 
(2) the application is complete; 
(3) the proposed wireless facility complies with all application federal, state, and local laws regulations, 
rules, restrictions, and conditions; and 
(4) the proposed wireless facility will be in compliance with all applicable Federal Communications 
Commission (“FCC”) rules and regulations relating to Radio Frequency (“RF”) emissions.  
SMMC Section 17.10.070(g) provides that an applicant, or property owners or residents within 500 feet of any 
proposed facility, may appeal the Director’s decision to approve or deny an application for a wireless permit 
with five calendar days of the decision to the City’s Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission 
(“Commission”).  However, appeals based on the environmental effects from RF emissions that comply with all 
applicable FCC regulations are not allowed.  The appellant bears the burden of proof to establish the basis for 
seeking a reversal of the Director’s decision.  The Commission’s decision shall be the final administrative 
decision for the City.
On October 22, 2024, Crown Castle (“Applicant”), working on behalf of Verizon Wireless, submitted an 
application for a wireless permit for a proposed wireless facility to be installed on an existing wood utility pole 
owned by PG&E, with PG&E Identification No. 110074648, and located approximately 400 feet west of the 
Warren Road/Hurlingham Avenue intersection (“Application”).
On January 17, 2025, the Director conditionally approved the Application.  On January 22, 2025, the City 
received identical appeals from six individuals (collectively “Appellants”) asserting 30 various reasons why the 
permit application should be denied.  The appeal hearing was subsequently held at a Commission regular 
meeting on February 12, 2025.
Section 2. Evidence Presented
A. City Staff Presentation
At the appeal hearing on this matter, City staff provided a presentation to the Commission which described the 
4 of 846

--- page 5 ---
2
proposed wireless facility, staff’s determination that the Application was complete, and a response to 
Appellants’ assertions.  City staff prepared an Agenda Report which provides a summary of staff’s responses to 
the Appeal, which is summarized below.  During its review, City staff also reviewed all possible alternative site 
locations and found the Applicant’s proposed location to be appropriate.  In its review and its presentation, City 
staff noted that freestanding poles are the least preferred option and only available upon a finding that all other 
existing poles are technically infeasible.  
In the presentation to the Commission, City staff also categorized the Appellants’ appeal categories, with 
responses to each, which includes:
1)
Category 1– Alternative Site Analysis.  
Appellants assert that the Applicant failed to show why only existing poles within the 200-foot 
radius from the proposed location are technically feasible and why other sites within a 500-foot 
radius is not technically feasible.  
Staff determined the Applicant provided sufficient information in the Alternative Site Analysis to 
approve the application because, based on staff’s own experience as well as consultation with a 
retained RF consultant, the reasonable range for these small wireless facilities is between 200 to 
300 feet, with 300 feet being under the most ideal conditions without physical interference.  
Here, the Applicant’s objective appears to be improved coverage and capacity in the immediate 
area of the proposed location and since the signal attenuates rapidly after 200 feet, it would not 
allow the Applicant to achieve this objective if other locations beyond 200 feet are considered.  
In addition, trees and other interferences limit the effective range in this area.
2)
Category 2 – Design Standards, Least Obtrusive
Appellants assert the proposed small wireless facility is highly obtrusive because of the height 
proposed, the location is conspicuous to pedestrians, and the design is inconsistent with the 
surrounding environment.
Staff determined the proposed small wireless facility is the least obtrusive because other 
existing poles within 500 feet are not technically feasible.  In addition, the height and location of 
the facility on the proposed pole is dictated by California Public Utilities Commission General 
Order 95 regulations (G0 95).  Due to various other installations on the proposed pole, the 
placement of the proposed small wireless facility is the only option available.  
3)
Category 3 – Environmental
Appellants assert the Application does not comply with CEQA and NEPA.
Application for a wireless permit to the City is exempt from CEQA review under CEQA Guidelines 
Sections 15302 and 15303, and an application to the City for a wireless permit is not subject to 
NEPA review. 
4)
Category 4 – Fire Risk
Appellants assert that the proposal facility presents an increased fire risk.
City staff does not believe these facilities present increased fire risks, and such a criteria is not 
required under the City’s 2021 Design Standards and Application Requirements.  In addition, 
City staff had previously reached out to San Mateo Consolidated Fire Department, which 
5 of 846

--- page 6 ---
3
indicated that there are no additional fire risks associated with these facilities.
5)
Category 5 – Incomplete or Errors in the Application
Appellants assert there is missing information in the Application such as a missing authorization 
from the pole owner (PG&E), an incomplete submittal in the required “Project Purpose and 
Technical Objective,” and expired engineer licenses on the stamped drawings of the proposed 
facility.
City staff found the Applicant submitted a complete application with all the required 
attachments which enabled staff to review and for the Director to make a decision.  The various 
information in the “Project Purpose and Technical Objective” was provided throughout the 
Application with specific references to the location, centerline height, equipment configuration, 
proposed elevation and plan views of the proposed site and equipment.  In addition, PG&E does 
not provide an authorization letter but the Application documents demonstrate that PG&E has 
authorized placement of the proposed facility.  Lastly, the engineers who stamped the 
documents were licensed at the time and still have current active licenses.   
6)
Category 6 – RF Emissions
Appellants assert Applicants failed to discuss if antenna tilts impact RF emission direction and 
distance.
City staff determined the 2021 Design Standards and Ordinance only requires the Applicant to 
analyze RF emissions based on the orientation of the antenna depicted in the plans, which the 
Applicant had done.  Applicants are not required to analyze RF emissions from alternative 
positions or angles, nor are they allowed to construct the proposed facility differently than as 
depicted in the Application.  The submitted RF report in the Application was reviewed by the 
City’s third-party RF consultant.
7)
Category 7 – Limited Exceptions
Appellants assert the Applicant failed to justify the necessity of limited exceptions granted to 
the 2021 Design Standards which allowed the proposed facility to be mounted on a side arm 
over the roadway at 4 feet, 9 inches, instead of a top mounted design.
City staff’s determined the Application provided sufficient justification to grant the limited 
exceptions to the 2021 Design Standards because other existing poles were found technically 
infeasible and the only existing pole available was limited by GO 95 regulations which precluded 
a pole-top mount design.  The only other option would have been consideration of a free-
standing pole; however, this option is the least preferred under the 2021 Design Standards and 
only allowed if all other existing poles were found technically infeasible.
8)
Category 8 – Miscellaneous
Appellants also asserted various miscellaneous points including: the Applicant failed to hold a 
community meeting; Applicant created a blight when they installed fiber facilities in the area; 
lower property values; that the indemnity provisions are not meaningful to protect the City; and 
the Applicant has had issues installing other facilities.
City staff has determined that a community  meaning is not required, the installation of fiber 
facilities is not relevant to this Application, property values are not considered as a criteria in the 
6 of 846

--- page 7 ---
4
2021 Design Standards, the indemnity provisions are sufficient, and any other issues with 
installation of facilities in the City unrelated to this Application are not germane to the City’s 
review and determination.
B.
Appellants’ Presentation
The Appellants asserted the following:
1)
An objection to the Sustainability and Commission’s jurisdiction to hear the instant appeal at issue.
2)
The Applicant failed to justify the limited exceptions granted including the side-mount extension over a 
street and in front of a window, which obstructs views.
3)
The Applicant failed to show alternatives are available and infeasible.
4)
The Applicant failed to show reasonable and clear objectives for their service, there are no alternatives 
that are technically feasible, and failing to approve the proposed location is a violation of Federal law.
5)
As to the design, the Applicant failed to show the exact dimensions why a pole-top design is not feasible 
or even the specific references to the GO 95 regulation precluding a pole-top design.
6)
A pole-top design is feasible.
7)
The Applicant failed to submit reasonable and clear service objectives, and the Applicant only provides a 
“big picture” objective rather than an explanation of how the proposed location is relevant or would 
work with other sites in the City. 
8)
The Applicant failed to submit information for the specific purpose of the proposed facility or any data 
supporting the 200-foot limitation or the relevant service objective that the proposed facility will serve.
9)
The Application does not discuss the manner of how it intends densify the network, and what the 
current density is. 
10) All the properties within the 200-foot radius are appealing approval of the Application.
11)  The Applicant failed to show an effective prohibition occurs if the proposed facility is denied.
12) The Applicant should be able to find a different location that can satisfy everyone.
13) Existing poles within island medians are more preferable.
C.
Applicant’s Presentation
The Applicant asserted the following:
1)
A pole-top design is not feasible. There is five feet at the top of the pole above secondary power lines. 
GO 95 Rule 38 requires clearance of six feet between an antenna mounted facility, including the mount, 
and the power facility below. There is not enough space at the top of the pole that is required pursuant 
to GO 95.
2)
The pole is not directly in front of any windows and proposed as far away from windows as feasible.
3)
Clarification that the technology is a small cell facility which is relatively small in dimension, and not a 
“tower.”
7 of 846

--- page 8 ---
5
4)
Under the 2018 Small Cell Order by the FCC, Applicants do not have to show some of the items 
discussed by Appellants, but instead that the Applicants can determine what their coverage objectives 
are.  
5)
The Applicant provided information that it intends to densify and increase capacity for their service in 
this specific area. 
6)
The type of spectrum as well as limitations on propagation beyond 200-feet for the equipment to be 
deployed support why the 200-foot radius was used and why alternative sites beyond 200-foot are not 
feasible.
7)
The 2018 Small Cell Order provides that materially inhibiting the established coverage objective is an 
effective prohibition.
8)
The Applicant has provided enough information to show the other sites are technically infeasible to 
support the Applicant’s coverage objectives and granting the appeal would materially inhibit the 
Applicant’s service objectives resulting in an effective prohibition.
9)
Existing poles within alternative island median locations are not feasible and will not allow for the 
Applicant to meet its service objectives.
10) PG&E no longer allows pole-top extensions.
11) The limited exceptions applied relate to limitations due to PG&E and GO 95 regulations.
Section 3. Findings of Fact
Based upon the evidence presented at the hearing on this matter, the Commission makes the following 
findings of fact:
1)
The Director conditionally approved the Application for a wireless permit on January 17, 2025, in 
conformance with SMMC Section 17.10.070(b), and the findings required therein.
2)
On January 22, 2025, the City received identical appeals from Appellants asserting various reasons why 
the permit application should be denied.
3)
The Appellants have the burden to establish a basis for reversal of the Director’s decision approving 
Application.
4)
City staff presented an articulated basis why the appeals should be denied.
5)
City staff’s recommendation as presented in the Agenda Report, inclusive of attachments, its 
presentation, and analysis are persuasive as to why the appeals should be denied and is hereby adopted 
by the Commission.
6)
The Commission is not convinced by the evidence presented by the Appellants.  Therefore, the 
Appellants failed to meet their burden to establish the Application was non-compliant with the City’s 
Ordinance and 2021 Design Standards and Application Requirements. 
7)
The Director’s decision is hereby adopted.
Section 4. Conclusion
Based upon the findings above, the Commission, by a 5-0 vote, deny the Appeals.  The Director’s 
8 of 846

--- page 9 ---
6
decision approving the Application is upheld.
The parties to this proceeding are informed that the time within which judicial review of this decision may be 
sought is governed by Section 1094.6 of the California Code of Civil Procedure.
Kimiko Narita, Chair, Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission

From: Ariel Strauss <ariel@alegal.info>

Sent: Wednesday, March 12, 2025 12:33 PM

To: Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission

Ce: Linh Nguyen

Subject: Proposed Edits to Statement of Decision for 124 Warren Rd (WC-2024-000243)
Attachments: REDLINE Draft Statement of Decision- 124 Warren.docx

Dear Chair Narita, Vice Chair Michael, Commissioner Kranz, Commissioner Robbins and Commissioner Rowinski:

Attached, please find my proposed revisions to the draft statement of decision for the 124 Warrant Rd. (WC-2024-
000243) appeal that was denied at the last hearing.

As noted in the document, my recommendation and request is to delete all of Section 2 (Evidence

Presented). Including this information is not typical for approving resolutions in other jurisdictions and is not required
by state or federal law. There is no need to take staff, Commission or members of the public's time seeking to accurately
reflect or summarize what occurred at the hearing. Also, the stated positions of parties each have varying levels of
credibility or influence to the Commission, which cannot be shown in the Section and regarding which there may be
disagreement among the Commissioners. The justification for the Commission's decision is the record presented to the
Commission and the recording of the hearing. Usually, that summary section contain a more general statement, like
this: “Based on the information set forth in the staff report, materials submitted by the parties to this appeal, comments
from the public, the hearing of February 12, 2025, and the public record as a whole, be it resolved that the Commission
finds that:”

| also wish to emphasize that a statement of decision is not a place to tidy up a messy hearing. It did not appear to me
that any Commissioner agreed on the record that Crown Castle provided "a reasonable and clearly defined technical
service objective to be achieved by the proposed wireless facility" (Sec. 3(1)(B)) or that Crown Castle provided "factual
reasons why all alternative locations and/or designs identified in the administrative record are not technically feasible or
potentially available[.]" (Sec. 3(1)(D).) Rather, Crown Castle insisted that the service objective was within 200 feet of the
pole and refused to explain the meaning or factual significance of the terms "densify or increase capacity" using the
relevant metrics (such as Mbps download speed, dBm signal strength, dropped calls, etc.). The Commission then
accepted the advice of staff that this was sufficient under federal law. If this is an accurate summary of what occurred,
then the statement of decision should reflect that.

| look forward to seeing the Commission’s action on this item.

Respectfully,
Ariel Strauss

Ariel Strauss

Statement of Decision by the San Mateo Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission in the Matter of an
Appeal of the Public Works Director’s Decision to Grant a Wireless Permit
(124 Warren Road, Permit # WC-2024-000243)

Section 1. Introduction

San Mateo Municipal Code (SMMC) Chapter 17.10 establishes reasonable, uniform and comprehensive
standards and procedures for wireless facilities deployment, construction, installation, collocation, modification,
operation, relocation, and removal within the City's public right-of-way, consistent with and to the extent

conditionally approve, or deny an application for a wireless permit upon a finding that:

(1) the applicant and the proposed wireless facility complies with all the requirements of SMMC Chapter
17.10, and the design standards and application requirements in effect at the time of application;

(2) the application is complete;

(3) the proposed wireless facility complies with all application federal, state, and local laws regulations,
rules, restrictions, and conditions; and

(4) the proposed wireless facility will be in compliance with all applicable Federal Communications
Commission (“FCC”) rules and regulations relating to Radio Frequency (“RF”) emissions.

SMMC Section 17.10.070(g) provides that an applicant, or property owners or residents within 500 feet of any
proposed facility, may appeal the Director’s decision to approve or deny an application for a wireless permit

Appellants assert Applicants failed to discuss if antenna tilts impact RF emission direction and
distance.

City staff determined the 2021 Design Standards and Ordinance only requires the Applicant to
analyze RF emissions based on the orientation of the antenna depicted in the plans, which the
Applicant had done. Applicants are not required to analyze RF emissions from alternative
positions or angles, nor are they allowed to construct the proposed facility differently than as
depicted in the Application. The submitted RF report in the Application was reviewed by the
City’s third-party RF consultant.

7) Category 7 —Limited Exceptions

Appellants assert the Applicant failed to justify the necessity of limited exceptions granted to
the 2021 Design Standards which allowed the proposed facility to be mounted ona side arm
over the roadway at 4 feet, 9 inches, instead of a top mounted design.

City staff's determined the Application provided sufficient justification to grant the limited
exceptions to the 2021 Design Standards because other existing poles were found technically
infeasible and the only existing pole available was limited by GO 95 regulations which precluded
a pole-top mount design. The only other option would have been consideration of a free-
standing pole; however, this option is the least preferred under the 2021 Design Standards and
only allowed if all other existing poles were found technically infeasible.

8) Category 8 ~ Miscellaneous

Appellants also asserted various miscellaneous points including: the Applicant failed to hold a
community meeting; Applicant created a blight when they installed fiber facilities in the area;
lower property values; that the indemnity provisions are not meaningful to protect the City; and
the Applicant has had issues installing other facilities.

City staff has determined that a community meaning is not required, the installation of fiber
facilities is not relevant to this Application, property values are not considered as a criteria in the
2021 Design Standards, the indemnity provisions are sufficient, and any other issues with

15 of 846


--- page 16 ---
installation of facilities in the City unrelated to this Application is not germane to the City’s
review and determination.

1) An objection to the Sustainability and Commission’s jurisdiction to hear the instant appeal at issue.

2) The Applicant failed to justify the limited exceptions granted including the side-mount extension over a
street and in-frontefawindew,which obstructs views from a window.

or even the specific references to the GO 95 regulation precluding a pole-top design.

“big picture” objective for the network rather than an explanation of how the proposed location is

SUBJECT:
Wireless Permit Approval at 16 Baldwin Ave (Permit# WC-2024-000241) - Appeals 
RECOMMENDATION:
Hold a public hearing to consider appeals from residents within 500 feet of the proposed site of a wireless permit 
application that was approved by the Director of Public Works under the City's 2021 Wireless Ordinance and Design 
Standards.
BACKGROUND:
On October 22, 2024, the City of San Mateo (“City”) staff received a Wireless Facilities Communications Permit Application 
(“Application”) from Crown Castle, working on behalf of Verizon for the installation of wireless communication facilities on 
an existing metal streetlight pole within the public right-of-way (Attachment 3). The location of the proposed wireless 
communications facility is in the downtown area, at the east corner of the El Camino Real/Baldwin Avenue intersection on 
an existing City-owned streetlight pole (Pole ID# 2805) within the public sidewalk. Attachment 1 shows the proposed 
facility’s location and photo simulation renderings.
 
This application was submitted prior to November 18, 2024, and is subject to the Ordinance and Design Standards 
effective at the time of submittal. Where the San Mateo Municipal Code (“SMMC”) or the City Design Standards and 
Application Requirements (“Design Standards”) are referenced, these are in reference to the 2021 SMMC language and 
Design Standards which were in effect at the time the application was submitted. These are included as attachments to 
this agenda report. The applicable SMMC and Design Standards are provided as Attachments 4 and 5.
 
As required by the SMMC Chapter 17.10, “Wireless Communications Facilities in the Public Right-of-Way,” Crown Castle 
must meet all requirements and design standards as outlined in SMMC Sections 17.10.040 and 17.10.050. This includes, 
but is not limited to, a full permit application form and providing mailed notices to nearby residents within a 500-foot 
radius of the proposed project site of the proposed wireless small cell facility. Based on the review of all the submitted 
documents, staff determined that the application and proposed installation meet the required conditions of approval as 
outlined in SMMC Chapter 17.10.
 
After its review, the City conditionally approved the Application on February 28, 2025. As required by the SMMC Section 
17.10.070, a decision notice was posted on February 28, 2025, on the City‘s Small Cell Infrastructure website. The notice 
advised residents of the Director of Public Works’ (“Director”) decision and allowed a 5-day appeal period.
 
 
 
Approval Authority
24 of 846

--- page 25 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
 
The Director’s decision to approve this Wireless Facilities Communications permit application and the criteria the 
Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission (“Commission”) must evaluate in its determination of whether to grant or 
deny any appeal is based on SMMC Section 17.10.070(b)(1-4), which is stated in pertinent part below. Note that “Chapter” 
refers to SMMC Chapter 17.10 and “RF” refers to radio frequency. 
 
Required Findings for Approval. The approval authority may approve or conditionally approve an application for a wireless 
permit submitted under this Chapter when the approval authority finds all the following:
 
1.
The applicant and the proposed wireless facility comply with all applicable requirements of this Chapter and the 
City Design Standards and Application Requirements (“Design Standards”); and
 
2.
The application is deemed complete by the Director; and
 
3.
The proposed wireless facility complies with all applicable federal, state and local laws, regulations, rules, 
restrictions and conditions, which includes without limitation, the California Building Standards Code or any local 
building codes; the Americans with Disabilities Act, and all applicable health and safety requirements, including 
Public Utilities Commission General Order 95, (and as these rules may be amended or superseded); General Plan 
and any applicable specific plan; the San Mateo Municipal Code; and any conditions or restrictions in any permit or 
other governmental approval issued by any public agency with jurisdiction over the project; and
 
4.
The applicant has demonstrated that its proposed wireless facility will be in compliance with all applicable FCC 
rules and regulations for human exposure to RF emissions.
 
Appeal to Wireless Permit
 
Pursuant to SMMC Section 17.10.070(g), the appellant on appeal has the burden of proof for establishing the basis for 
seeking the reversal of the permit approval.
 
The City received identical appeals from Mary Bianco, Kevin Lewis, and Senovia Grismore and George Grismore 
(collectively “Appellants”), all of whom authorized Irena Mavridis and Lindsay Raike to appear on their behalf.  The 
Appellants submitted six items as the basis for their appeal (“Basis Items”)(Attachment 2). 
 
Pursuant to SMMC Section 17.10.070(g), the Commission shall hold a public hearing to consider and act on the appeal de 
novo and in accordance with the required findings by issuing a decision at the hearing.
 
Staff Review
 
Staff reviewed the wireless permit application for conformance to SMMC Section 17.10.070(b)(1-4).
 
Staff has summarized the Basis Items below. The text in italics below are exact quotes from the appellant’s material. Any 
references to standards or regulations within the quote are included as stated in the original text and do not imply 
verification, endorsement, or acceptance of their accuracy or applicability. The original structure of these Basis Items can 
be found in Attachment 2. Therefore, the appropriate scope of appeal is as follows:
 
Basis 1: Environmental 

The Director has not made a finding that the proposed wireless facility at 16 Baldwin Ave complies with all 
applicable federal, state and local laws, regulations, rules, restrictions and conditions.

The City’s outside counsel responded that there were no requirements for the City to request documentation of the 
NEPA process or whether an exemption from NEPA applies, or even to ask about NEPA.  That response was 
contrary to the Code citation above, which requires the Director to find that the proposed wireless facility complies 
with all applicable law.
25 of 846

--- page 26 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO

The applicant has not met the burden of proof in demonstrating compliance with all applicable federal, state and 
local laws, regulations, rules, restrictions and conditions.
Basis 1 Determination: Staff determined the applicant fulfilled the application requirements. SMMC 17.10.070(b)(3) states 
that the proposed wireless facility shall comply with all applicable federal, state and local laws, regulations, rules, 
restrictions and conditions. National Environmental Policy Act (NEPA) review is triggered when a federal agency is involved 
and is not applicable to the City’s application review process. The City of San Mateo’s decisions, actions, and projects must 
comply with the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), and under CEQA, applications of this nature are categorically 
exempt under section 15301, 15302, and 15303.
 
Basis 2: Design Standards – Location Preferences 

Crown Castle Has Not Made a Factual Showing That All More Preferred Locations are Technically Infeasible, and Its 
Application is Incomplete.

Conclusory statements that a particular alternative is unacceptable, infeasible, unavailable or not in accordance 
with the development standards in Chapter 17.10 will be deemed incomplete.

Crown Castle has offered only conclusory statements in its alternative sites analysis, which statements are deemed 
incomplete per the City's Design Standards. Further, Verizon has stated publicly that 28,000 MHz RF emissions 
extend 3,000 feet.  
Basis 2 Determination: Staff determined there was sufficient information in the alternative site analysis to approve the 
application. One of the appellants’ main positions is the applicant failed to demonstrate the proposed equipment is indeed 
limited to 200-ft. The applicant provided justification in the alternative site analysis about its technology limitations and is 
consistent with prior wireless permit applications to the City, and also consistent with the City’s and its 3rd party radio 
frequency electromagnetic energy (RF-EME) consultant’s understanding of technology limitations in the industry. Three 
other technically feasible locations are noted to be less preferred based on Design Standard #1 – Least Obtrusive because, 
while all four technically feasible locations are considered the same residential zoning preference, the proposed location is 
located farthest from existing buildings which staff considers least obtrusive. All other locations reference the specific City 
Design Standards, General Order 95 (GO-95) requirements, or PG&E standards that make them technically infeasible.
 
 
Basis 3: Incomplete or Errors in Application

This [Proposed Project, Network] statement is inaccurate as this is expired information. Per the city attorney, 
Crown Castle’s new proposed network is now 50 antenna nodes, not the stated 197.

False Statements in Sections III-f and III-g.

Crown Castle repeats the claim that "coverage" is one of the project objectives. Therefore, Drive Test Data is 
required per Section III-g… The application is invalid without the Drive Test Data as required by San Mateo code.
Basis 3 Determination: Staff reviewed all the basis items in Basis 3 and determined the applicant submitted a complete 
application with all required attachments that meet the application requirements. The applicant provided the required 
information as listed in the application checklist. The applicant described the project’s purpose. Per the application 
checklist, drive tests are not required. All required documents were provided and included sufficient information.
 
Basis 4: Fire Risk

The Proposed Wireless Facility Presents a Fire Hazard. The pole location at 16 Baldwin Ave presents a fire hazard 
dangerously close to peoples' homes.

The risk of fires caused by cell facilities placed near homes will be yet another reason for insurance carriers to 
decline to cover homes.
Basis 4 Determination: Staff determined there are no requirements under the 2021 Wireless Small Cell Design Standards 
and Ordinance to assess fire risk. In addition, staff previously reached out to the San Mateo Consolidated Fire (SMC Fire) 
Fire Marshall who did not believe any additional fire risks are associated with these wireless small cell facilities. 
 
Basis 5: Design Standards – Least Obtrusive

The pole located at 16 Baldwin Ave is situated directly in front of a retirement home, adjacent to an elementary 
school, and near Mills Health Center.
26 of 846

--- page 27 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO

It is aesthetically offensive and jarring to place wireless facilities directly adjacent to residential landscaping.
 
Basis 5 Determination: Staff determined the proposed location is in in compliance with Design Standard #1 - Least 
Obtrusive. The applicant demonstrated only three other existing poles within 500 feet are technically feasible in the 
Alternative Sites Analysis. Three other technically feasible locations are noted to be less preferred based on Design 
Standard #1 – Least Obtrusive because, while all four technically feasible locations are considered the same residential 
zoning preference, the proposed location is located farthest from existing buildings which staff considers least obtrusive. 
Therefore, the proposed location is the least obtrusive among technically feasible locations.  
 
Basis 6 – Miscellaneous

Crown Castle Did Not Hold Neighborhood Meetings.

[The proposed location is] mere steps from the St. Matthews Episcopal Day School courtyard where children play.

Crown Castle lied to the S&I Commission and San Mateo residents regarding its intentions with respect to facility 
placement.
Basis 6 Determination: Per the 2021 Design Standards, a neighborhood meeting is not required. All other positions are not 
applicable to the decision of this application.
 
Based on the review of the Crown Castle application and the above, staff believe Crown Castle has met the requirements 
of the 2021 Wireless Ordinance and 2021 Design Standards and Application Requirements. 
 
Therefore, Staff recommends the Commission deny the appeal and adopt a Statement of Decision denying the appeal. A 
draft Statement of Decision is attached as Attachment 6 and will be updated for the Commission’s review and adoption at 
the conclusion of the appeal hearing.
BUDGET IMPACT:
This public hearing to consider resident appeals does not have a direct impact on the City's Budget other than costs 
associated with staff time which are paid for by the permit applicant.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This appeal is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

The application states:

b. The Proposed Project

i. The Network.

“Crown Castle proposes developing its SCN network with approximately one-hundred and ninety-seven new (197) antenna nodes in
the ROW (the "Project") in the City of San Mateo ("Network").

All proposed nodes qualify as Small Wireless Facilities as defined in 47 C.F.R § 1.6002(|).

Specifically, this application proposes one antenna node submitted to the City of San Mateo for a Wireless Permit by the Department
Public Works. Completion of the Project will provide needed wireless broadband and communications services and the addition of
critical network capacity to throughout portions of the City of San Mateo ("Service Area(s)"). Where feasible, each of the 197 nodes
comprising the SCN will utilize existing vertical elements in the ROW, including utility poles and city-owned Streetlights.

Each SCN node receives an optical signal from a central hub and distributes the signal to the antenna nodes via fiber optic cable. The
optical signal is then propagated from the SCN nodes in the form of radio frequency transmissions. Distribution of signal from the hub
to the low-power, low-profile antenna nodes, allows carriers to offload service capacity and provide wireless communications and data
services to areas otherwise difficult to reach with conventional wireless telecommunications facilities.

By using existing streetlight, traffic signal poles, and utility pole attachments whenever possible, the Project seeks to reduce the
addition of new vertical elements, thereby minimizing intrusions.”

This statement is inaccurate as this is expired information. Per the city attorney, Crown Castle’s new proposed network is now 50
antenna nodes, not the stated 197.

False Statements in Sections Ill-f and Ill-g clearly states the purpose is to address coverage gaps as shown by these words pulled from
the application “to level that allows adequate in-building coverage.”

“f, Selection Criteria for Node Site Location.

“Each node of the Network is necessary to support a degradation of service due to overload on the system. The need to maintain
minimum quality of service to a level that allows adequate in-building coverage and to address growing capacity demands is
underscored by the greater numbers.”

In another instance in Section II, Crown Castle repeats the claim that "coverage" is one of the project objectives

Therefore, Drive Test Data is required per Section Ill-g. See the statement "addressing a coverage gap is not a technical objective,”
which directly conflicts with section Ill, and therefore is false.

The application is invalid without the Drive Test Data as required by San Mateo code

The Proposed Facility Presents Unsafe Conditions, and the City has the Absolute Power to Deny the Application on this Basis.

(a) The Proposed Wireless Facility Presents a Fire Hazard. The pole location at 16 Baldwin Ave presents a fire hazard dangerously close
to peoples' homes.

Last winter, an unprecedented number of trees in San Mateo toppled over due to atmospheric rivers following years of drought, and
we experience very high winds from time to time throughout the year. The risk of these types of events will continue to be
exacerbated by climate change. Los Angeles just weeks ago experienced devastating fires with loss of lives and homes. Insurance
carriers are already pulling out all across California due to the heightened fire risks. The risk of fires caused by cell facilities placed near
homes will be yet another reason for insurance carriers to decline to cover homes in San Mateo causing significant and unnecessary
financial hardship to homeowners near 16 Baldwin Ave.

As described in an Aspen Times opinion article dated April 13, 2021, Susan Foster, writer and honorary firefighter with the San Diego
Fire Department, "cautions cities to establish residential setbacks from all wireless installations so that people have time to escape in
the event of a fire." The same article further states: "According to Tony P. Simmons, P. E., an electrical engineer who is a subject matter
expert on electrical safety in California and Nevada, 'Many people are not aware that electrical equipment, including all cell towers and
5G small cell sites, pose a fire threat that must be mitigated by a recognized electrical fire safety expert. Every electrical device is going
to fail at some point. The goal is to ensure that failures do not imperil life, health and property."

Guest commentary: Is 5G a potential fire hazard?

“Crown Castle proposes developing its SCN network with approximately one-hundred and ninety-seven new (197) antenna nodes in
the ROW (the "Project") in the City of San Mateo ("Network").

All proposed nodes qualify as Small Wireless Facilities as defined in 47 C.F.R § 1.6002(I).

Specifically, this application proposes one antenna node submitted to the City of San Mateo for a Wireless Permit by the Department
Public Works. Completion of the Project will provide needed wireless broadband and communications services and the addition of
critical network capacity to throughout portions of the City of San Mateo ("Service Area(s)"). Where feasible, each of the 197 nodes
comprising the SCN will utilize existing vertical elements in the ROW, including utility poles and city-owned Streetlights.

Each SCN node receives an optical signal from a central hub and distributes the signal to the antenna nodes via fiber optic cable. The
optical signal is then propagated from the SCN nodes in the form of radio frequency transmissions. Distribution of signal from the hub
to the low-power, low-profile antenna nodes, allows carriers to offload service capacity and provide wireless communications and data
services to areas otherwise difficult to reach with conventional wireless telecommunications facilities.

By using existing streetlight, traffic signal poles, and utility pole attachments whenever possible, the Project seeks to reduce the
addition of new vertical elements, thereby minimizing intrusions.”

This statement is inaccurate as this is expired information. Per the city attorney, Crown Castle’s new proposed network is now 50
antenna nodes, not the stated 197.

False Statements in Sections Ill-f and Ill-g clearly states the purpose is to address coverage gaps as shown by these words pulled from
the application “to level that allows adequate in-building coverage.”

“f, Selection Criteria for Node Site Location.

“Each node of the Network is necessary to support a degradation of service due to overload on the system. The need to maintain
minimum quality of service to a level that allows adequate in-building coverage and to address growing capacity demands is
underscored by the greater numbers.”

In another instance in Section II, Crown Castle repeats the claim that "coverage" is one of the project objectives

Therefore, Drive Test Data is required per Section Ill-g. See the statement "addressing a coverage gap is not a technical objective,”
which directly conflicts with section Ill, and therefore is false.

The application is invalid without the Drive Test Data as required by San Mateo code

The Proposed Facility Presents Unsafe Conditions, and the City has the Absolute Power to Deny the Application on this Basis.

(a) The Proposed Wireless Facility Presents a Fire Hazard. The pole location at 16 Baldwin Ave presents a fire hazard dangerously close
to peoples' homes.

Last winter, an unprecedented number of trees in San Mateo toppled over due to atmospheric rivers following years of drought, and
we experience very high winds from time to time throughout the year. The risk of these types of events will continue to be
exacerbated by climate change. Los Angeles just weeks ago experienced devastating fires with loss of lives and homes. Insurance
carriers are already pulling out all across California due to the heightened fire risks. The risk of fires caused by cell facilities placed near
homes will be yet another reason for insurance carriers to decline to cover homes in San Mateo causing significant and unnecessary
financial hardship to homeowners near 16 Baldwin Ave.

As described in an Aspen Times opinion article dated April 13, 2021, Susan Foster, writer and honorary firefighter with the San Diego
Fire Department, "cautions cities to establish residential setbacks from all wireless installations so that people have time to escape in
the event of a fire." The same article further states: "According to Tony P. Simmons, P. E., an electrical engineer who is a subject matter
expert on electrical safety in California and Nevada, 'Many people are not aware that electrical equipment, including all cell towers and
5G small cell sites, pose a fire threat that must be mitigated by a recognized electrical fire safety expert. Every electrical device is going
to fail at some point. The goal is to ensure that failures do not imperil life, health and property."

Guest commentary: Is 5G a potential fire hazard?

TO: Secretary of the Sustainability & Infrastructure Commission

Per San Mateo Municipal Code Section 17.10.070(g), the wireless permit applicant or any person who is a property owner or
resident within 500' of the project site may appeal any decision by the Director to approve or deny an application for a wireless
permit. Appeals must be filed with the Secretary of the Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission within five calendar days
following the Director's decision. Appeals from an approval will not be permitted to the extent that the appeal is based on
environmental effects from RF emissions that comply with all applicable FCC regulations.

PUBLIC NOTICE

Wireless Permit Application Submitted

Near 16 BALDWIN AVE, San Mateo, CA 94401
Pole ID #: 2805

Dear Property Owner or Resident:

This is a notice that Crown Castle has submitted a wireless permit application to the City of San Mateo Public
Works Department for a small wireless facility to be located on an existing streetlight pole with an associated
meter pedestal in the public right-of-way at the location below. Construction for the site is currently anticipated to
begin January, 2025 and end by March, 2025.

A “small wireless facility” is a low-powered, compact device used to provide wireless communications services.
Crown Castle will be the owner and operator of the proposed facility, but Verizon, the carrier customer, will be
using this specific facility to improve the coverage and capacity for their network in your neighborhood.

The application is currently under review by Public Works and a decision has not been made.

Location of Proposed Facility . Photo Simulation of Proposed Facility

Questions and comments can be sent to the contacts below until a City Decision Notice is posted:

Applicant Contact City of San Mateo Contact

Crown Castle Public Works — Permitting Division

Taylor Blanford — Permitting Agent 330 W. 20" Avenue, San Mateo, CA 94403
1300 Clay Street, Suite 325, Oakland, CA 94612 pwencroachment@cityofsanmateo.org
Taylor.Blanford@kimley-horn.com (650) 522-7300

(510) 210-3221

The City will act on the application without a public hearing. Members of the public interested in receiving
information on application decisions should sign up for notifications on the Small Cell Infrastructure website,
as no additional notices will be mailed.

SMALL CELL PERMITTING INFO HERE > hitps://www.cityofsanmateo.org/3865/

APPEALS
Appeals may be filed by the Applicant or any person
who is a property owner or resident within 500-feet of
the project site within five (5) calendar days after the
Decision Notice. The appeal shall be scheduled for
public hearing on the agenda for the next regular or
special meeting of the Sustainability and
Infrastructure Commission, or otherwise within a time
frame needed to comply with all applicable state or
federal laws.
The FCC does not allow appeals when based
solely on the environmental effects from radio
frequency emissions that are compliant with
applicable FCC regulations and guidelines.

RE: FAA Filing for Wireless Facilities

Dear City of San Mateo Public Works,

Crown Castle’s proposed Small Wireless Communication Facilities do not require the completion and
filing of FAA Form 7460 due to this project not meeting the requirements of the Federal Aviation Code Title 14,
Chapter 1, Subchapter E, Part 77. Crown Castle’s proposed Small Wireless Communication Facilities do not meet
the FAA requirements for facilities that must file with the FAA which is listed below.

§ 77.9 — Any person/organization who intends to sponsor any of the following construction or
alterations must notify the Administrator of the FAA:
e Any construction or alteration exceeding 200 ft above ground level
e Any construction or alteration
o within 20,000 ft of a public use or military airport which exceeds a 100:1 surface from any point on
the runway of each airport with at least one runway more than 3,200 ft.
o within 10,000 ft of a public use or military airport which exceeds a 50:1 surface from any point on
the runway of each airport with its longest runway no more than 3,200 ft.
within 5,000 ft of a public use heliport which exceeds a 25:1 surface
o Any highway, railroad or other traverse way whose prescribed adjusted height would exceed that
above noted standards
o When requested by the FAA
o Any construction or alteration located on a public use airport or heliport regardless of height or
location

Furthermore, the FAA Code states that one does not need to file notice for construction or alteration of any
object that will be shielded by existing structures of a permanent and substantial nature or by natural terrain or
topographic features of equal or greater height and will be located in the congested area of a city, town, or
settlement where the shielded structure will not adversely affect safety in air navigation. All of Crown Castle’s
proposed locations meet this requirement.

The pathway to possible.
CrownCastle.com

PUBLIC UTILITIES COMMISSION
505 Van Ness Avenue
San Francisco CA 94102-3298

To: Telecommunications Carrier Filing Advice Letter
From: Telecommunications Division PAL Coordinator

Subject: Your Advice Letter Filing

The Telecommunications Division of the California Public Utilities Commission has
processed your recent Advice Letter (AL) filing and is returning an AL status certificate for
your records.

The AL status certificate indicates:

Advice Letter Number

Name of Filer

CPUC Corporate ID number of Filer

Subject of Filing

Date Filed

Disposition of Filing (Accepted, Rejected, Withdrawn, etc.)

Effective Date of Filing

Other Miscellaneous Information (e.g., Resolution, if applicable, etc.)

The Telecommunications Division has made no changes to your copy of the Advice Letter
Filing; please review your Advice Letter Filing with the information contained in the AL
status certificate, and update your Advice Letter and tariff records accordingly.

All inquiries to the California Public Utilities Commission on the status of your Advice
Letter Filing will be answered by Telecommunications Division staff based on the
information contained in the Telecommunications Division's PAL database from which the
AL status certificate is generated. If you have any questions on this matter please contact
the:

Telecommunications Division PAL Coordinator at (415) 703-1565, or by
e-mail to td_pal_coordinator@cpuc.ca.gov

OPINION

By this decision, we grant the petitions for certificates of public
convenience and necessity (CPCN) to operate as facilities-based competitive local
carriers (CLCs) and to offer resold local exchange services within the territories
of Pacific Bell (Pacific), GTE California Incorporated (GTEC), Roseville
Telephone Company (RTC), and Citizens Telephone Company (CTC), for those
petitioners as set forth in Appendix B of this decision, subject to the terms and
conditions included herein. We also grant petitioners’ requests for intrastate
interLocal Access and Transport Areas (interLATA) and intraLATA authority on |

a statewide basis as designated in Appendix B.
I. Background

We initially established rules for entry of facilities-based CLCs in Decision
(D.) 95-07-054. Under those procedures, we processed a group of candidates that
filed petitions for CPCNs by September 1, 1995, and granted authority effective
January 1, 1996, for qualifying CLCs to provide facilities-based competitive local

-1-

115 of 846


--- page 116 ---
R.95-04-043, 1.95-04-044 ALJ/TRP/avs a

exchange service in the territories of Pacificand GTEC. We authorized CLCs
seeking to provide resale-based services to begin operations on March 1, 1996.
We further advised prospective entrants that any filings from nonqualifying
CLCs, and any filing for CLC operating authority made after September 1, 1995,
would be treated as standard applications and processed in the normal course of
the Commission’s business.

By D.96-12-020, effective January 1, 1997, we instituted quarterly
processing cycles for granting CPCN authority for facilities-based CLCs in order
to streamline the approval process for these particular carriers. Since we had
been processing the environmental impact review required under the California
Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) on a consolidated basis for groups of
qualifying facilities-based CLCs, we concluded in D.96-12-020 that it would be
more efficient and consistent to process other aspects of the CLC filings on a
consolidated basis, as well. Accordingly, we directed that any CLC filing on or
after January 1, 1997, for facilities-based CPCN authority was to make its filing in
the form of a petition to be docketed in Investigation (I.) 95-04-044 that would be
processed quarterly on a consolidated basis. CLCs seeking only resale authority
continued to file individual applications.

On September 24, 1997, we adopted D.97-09-115 in which we extended the
coverage of our adopted rules for local exchange competition to include the
service territories of California’s two midsized local exchange carriers (MSLECs),
RTC and CTC. In that decision, we also authorized candidates seeking CLC
CPCN authority within the MSLECs’ territories to immediately begin making
filings following the applicable entry rules previously adopted in D.95-07-054
and subsequent decisions. Specifically, requests for CLC CPCN authority for
facilities-based service were to be filed in the form of a petition docketed in

1.95-04-044, while resellers have sought authority through applications. In

-2-

116 of 846


--- page 117 ---
»

_ R.95-04-043, 1.95-04-044 ALJ/TRP/avs

D.98-01-055, we approved the first group of petitions for facilities-based CPCNs
to offer local exchange service within the MSLEC territories. .

In this decision, we approve CPCNs for those facilities-based CLCs which
filed petitions during the first quarter of 1999 and satisfied all applicable rules for
certification as established in Rulemaking (R.) 95-04-043. The Petitioners
identified in Appendix B will be authorized to begin offering service upon the
filing of tariffs and compliance with the terms and conditions set forth in this

order.
ll. CEQA Review

We have reviewed the petitions for compliance with CEQA. CEQA
requires the Commission to assess the potential environmental impact of a
project in order that adverse effects are avoided, alternatives are investigated,
and environmental quality is restored or enhanced to the fullest extent possible.
To achieve this objective, Rule 17.1 of the Commission’s Rules requires the
proponent of any project subject to Commission approval to submit with the
petition for approval of such project a Proponent’s Environmental Assessment
(PEA). The PEA is used by the Commission to focus on any impacts of the
project which may be of concern, and prepare the Commission’s Initial Study to
determine whether the project needs a Negative Declaration or an Environmental
Impact Report (EIR). |

Based on its assessment of the facilities-based petitions and PEAs, the
Commission staff prepared a Negative Declaration and Initial Study generally
describing the facilities-based Petitioners’ projects and their potential
environmental effects. The Negative Declaration prepared by the Commission
staff is considered a Mitigated Negative Declaration (MND). This means that,
although the initial study identified potentially significant impacts, revisions

117 of 846


--- page 118 ---
R.95-04-043, 1.95-04-044 ALJ/TRP/avs '

which mitigate the impacts to a less than significant level have been agreed to by
the Petitioners. (Pub. Res. Code § 21080(c)(2).)-

A. Results of the Negative Declaration

On April 29, 1999, the Negative Declaration and Initial Study were sent
to various city and county planning agencies, as well as public libraries
throughout the state for review and comment by May 28, 1999. The Commission
staff prepared a public notice which announced the preparation of the draft
negative declaration, the locations where it was available for review, and the
deadline for written comments. The public notice was advertised in newspapers
throughout the state. The draft Negative Declaration was also submitted to the
Governor's Office of Planning and Research where it was circulated to affected
state agencies for review and comment. | =

Public comments on the draft Negative Declaration were reviewed and
answered, as necessary. The Commission staff then finalized the MND covering
all facilities-based CLC petitions listed in Appendix B. The finalized MND

includes a list of mitigation measures with which the CLCs must comply as a

oy

condition of their CPCN authority. The MND includes a Mitigation Monitoring
Plan to ensure that the mitigation measures are followed. and implemented as
intended. A copy of the MND is attached to this decision as Appendix D. We
hereby approve the MND as finalized by staff. Concurrently with our approval
of the MND, we grant the request of the Petitioners in Appendix B for CPCN

authority subject to the terms and conditions set forth in our order below.
B. Required Payment of CEQA Deposit

Commission Decision 97-04-046 stipulates that all petitioners for CLC
authority must submit with their filing an initial payment of $2000 to cover

CEQA costs. The $2000 payment is used to cover the Commission’s costs for

-4-

118 of 846


--- page 119 ---
. R.95-04-043, 1.95-04-044 ALJ/TRP/avs

preparing and publishing the Mitigated Negative Declaration for each qualifying
petitioner, as required by CEQA law. As of the date of this order, the
. Commission has received payment of the required $2000 deposit from each of

the CLCs, as identified in Appendix B.

Ill. Review of CPCN Petitions

A. Overview
The CLC petitions have been reviewed for compliance with the
certification-and-entry rules (Rules) adopted in Appendices A and B of
D.95-07-054 and subsequent decisions in R.95-04-043/1.95-04-044. Consistent
with our goal of promoting a competitive market as rapidly as possible, we are
granting authority to all of the facilities-based CLCs that filed during the first
quarter of 1999 and met the Rules. The Rules are intended to protect the public

against unqualified or unscrupulous carriers, while also encouraging and easing

the entry of CLC providers to promote the rapid growth of competition.
Petitioners had to demonstrate that they possessed the requisite

" managerial qualifications, technical competence, and financial resources to
provide facilities-based local exchange service. Petitioners were also required to
submit proposed tariffs which conform to the consumer protection rules set forth
in Appendix B of D.95-07-054. In response to a notice of tariff deficiencies, the
various petitioners submitted tariff corrections. Except for the outstanding
deficiencies noted in Appendix C, the petitioners’ proposed tariffs are found to
be satisfactory with no deficiencies noted.

_ As prescribed in Rule 4.B.(1), prospective facilities-based CLCs must

also show that they possess a minimum of $100,000 in cash or cash-equivalent
resources, as defined in the Rules. In.order to demonstrate that they possess the

requisite financial resources, petitioners submitted copies of recent financial

-5-

119 of 846


--- page 120 ---
R.95-04-043, 1.95-04-044 ALJ/TRP/avs

statements. Because the financial statements contain commercially sensitive
information, the petitioners filed motions for limited protective orders to restrict
the financial statements and related documents containing commercially
sensitive information from public disclosure pursuant to General Order

(GO) 66-C. We grant those motions as prescribed in our order below.

Based upon our review, we conclude that each of the facilities-based
Petitioners identified in Appendix B, has satisfactorily complied with our
certification requirements for entry, including the consumer protection rules set
forth in D.95-07-054, subject to correcting any tariff deficiencies in Appendix C,
payment of the required CEQA deposit, and satisfying the additional conditions
set forth in the ordering paragraphs below. Accordingly, we grant these
Petitioners authority to offer facilities-based and resold local exchange service
within the territories of Pacific and GTEC and, where requested, within the CTC
and RTC territories. We also grant the statewide inter- and intraLATA authority
as requested. |

Pursuant to D.97-09-115, CLC resale authority within the RTC and CTC
territories was authorized to become effective on or after April 1, 1998. As we
stated in D.97-09-115, until the time that tariffed wholesale discouni rates are
adopted for RTC and CTC, individual CLCs certificated to resell local service
within the CTC/RTC territories may enter into negotiations with each of the
MSLECs to seek agreement on an interim wholesale discount rate. Disputes over
the terms of resale arrangements may be submitted to the Commission for
arbitration pursuant to the provisions of Section 252(b)(1) of the

Telecommunication Act of 1996 and Commission Resolution ALJ-174.

_ R.95-04-043, 1.95-04-044 ALJ/TRP/avs

B. Motion of DSLnet

DSLnet Communications, LLC (‘DSLnet”), attempted to file a petition
(# 142) for CLC local exchange authority on March 31, 1999, with the intention of
being included in the Commission’s quarterly “batch” review of such petitions
filed during the first quarter of 1999. However, DSLnet subsequently learned
that, due to certain confusion surrounding whether DSLnet'’s Petition was
complete for purposes of the Commission’s review, the Commission did not
technically accept DSLnet’s petition until April 13, 1999. As a result, it is now too
late for DSLnet’s Petition to be included in the Commission’s quarterly review
process for such petitions filed during the first quarter of 1999, at least to the
extent DSLnet seeks facilities-based authority.

Nonetheless, in order to allow DSLnet to initiate competitive
telecommunications service in California as soon as possible, DSLnet filed a
motion on May 4, 1999, asking the Commission to: (1) immediately consider the
portion of DSLnet'’s Petition seeking authority to resell local exchange
telecommunications services, and (2) consider the portion of DSLnet’s Petition
seeking facilities-based authority in the Commission’s quarterly review process
for Petitions filed during the second quarter of 1999.

No party has objected to the motion of DSLnet. We consider the
request of DSLnet for consideration of the resale portion of its petition in the
current quarterly review to be reasonable, under the circumstances and shall
grant it.

Due to the timing requirements relating to the Mitigated Negative
Declaration, DSLnet’s request for facilities-based authority cannot be considered
during the current quarter, but shall be deferred to the subsequent quarterly

review period.

R.95-04-043, 1.95-04-044 ALJ/TRP/avs
IV. Compliance With Section 311

In compliance with Pub. Util. Code Section 311 (g)(2), this is an
uncontested matter in which the decision grants the relief requested.

Accordingly, pursuant to Pub. Util. Code Section 311(g)(2), the otherwise

applicable 30-day period for public review and comment is being waived.

Findings of Fact

1. Nine petitioners filed requests during the first quarter of 1999 seeking a

CPCN to provide competitive local exchange services in the territories of various
' California incumbent local exchange carriers as set forth in Appendix B.

2. An additional petitioner, DSLnet attempted to file during the first quarter,
but the filing was not actually docketed until April 13, 1999. DSLnet
subsequently filed an uncontested motion seeking to have its 1equest for CLC
resale authority to be considered as part of the first quarterly group of CLCs.

3. No protests to the CLC petitioners have been filed.

4. A hearing is not required.

5. By prior Commission decisions, we authorized competition in providing
local exchange telecommunications service within the service territories of
Pacific, GTEC, RTC, and CTC for carriers meeting specified criteria.

6. The Petitioners listed in Appendix B have demonstrated that each of them
has a minimum of $100,000 in cash or cash equivalent reasonably liquid and
readily available to meet its start-up expenses.

7. Petitioners’ technical experience is demonstrated by supporting
documentation which provides summary biographies of their key management
personnel.

8. Except as noted in Appendix C, Petitioners have each submitted a

complete draft of their initial tariff which complies with the requirements

ORDER

IT IS ORDERED that:

1. A certificate of public convenience and necessity (CPCN), shall be granted
to each of the Petitioners listed in Appendix B (Petitioners) to permit each of
them to operate as a facilities-based provider of competitive local exchange
telecommunications services, as a reseller of competitive local exchange
telecommunications services within the service territories as noted in
Appendix B and, as a statewide nondominant interexchange carrier (NDIEC), as
noted in Appendix B, contingent on compliance with the terms identified in’
Appendix B and in the remainder of this order.

2. Each Petitioner shall file a written acceptance of the certificate granted in
this proceeding prior to commencing service.

3. a. The Petitioners are authorized to file with this Commission tariff
schedules for the provision of competitive local exchange, intraLATA (Local |
Access Transport Area) toll and intrastate interLATA services, as applicable. The
Petitioners may not offer these services until tariffs are on file, and until any

applicable deficiencies as noted in Appendix C have been corrected. Petitioners’

approval by the Telecommunications Division.

b. The Petitioners are competitive local carriers (CLCs). The effectiveness
of each of their future tariffs is subject to the schedules set forth in Decision
(D.) 95-07-054, Appendix A, § 4E.

A. “E. CLCs shall be subject to the following tariff and
contract-filing, revision and service-pricing standards:

“(1) Uniform rate reductions for existing tariff services shall
become effective on five (5) working days’ notice to the
Commission. Customer notification is not required for rate _
decreases.

“(2) Uniform major rate increases for existing tariff services shall
become effective on thirty (30) days’ notice to the
Commission, and shall require bill inserts, or a message on
the bill itself, or first class mail notice to customers at least
30 days in advance of the pending rate increase.

“(3) Uniform minor rate increases, as defined in D.95-07-054,
shall become effective on not less than five (5) working
days’ notice to the Commission. Customer notification is

- not required for such minor rate increases.

“(4) Advice letter filing for new services and for all other types
of tariff revisions, except changes in text not affecting rates
or relocations of text in the tariff schedules, shall become
effective on forty (40) days’ notice to the Commission.

“(5) Advice letter filings revising the text or location of text
material which do not result in an increase in any rate or
charge shall become effective on not less than five (5) days’
notice to the Commission.

“(6) Contracts shall be subject to GO 96-A rules for NDIECs,
except interconnection contracts.
