--- page 808 ---
would “provide improved service coverage to an area of 1.6 square miles and a population of
2,420 residents” but without “the underlying factual basis for these statements” does not
establish an effective prohibition.** In 2023, a federal judge granted summary judgment for West
Covina and against AT&T because AT&T “declined to supply information regarding the number
of residents who might benefit from the Proposed Facility.”*> The applicant must have some
meaningful explanation of the actual, real-world impact of the denial for customers. In order to
determine whether federal preemption applies, the City may demand that the applicant describes

how the facilities will be used and their relevance to the network.

Regardless of whether the “material inhibition” or “least intrusive means” test is used,
Crown Castle’s refusal to provide basic information is fatal to any claim. It has the burden to
show that it is in fact “densifying a wireless network, introducing new services or otherwise
improving service capabilities” in a significant way. It is not credible that Crown Castle is going
through all this time, effort and expense to provide service to a couple of houses in a 200-foot
radius. It is not enough that Crown Castle just parrot the words of the FCC order to gain the right
to override the City’s Ordinance and Policies. Without factual support, Crown Castle cannot

show that any “inhibition” is in fact “material.”
I. Verizon Already Offers Good Mobile Broadband in the Area

Crown Castle is not a service provider. It obtains site permits and builds facilities on
behalf of wireless carriers. This site is for Verizon. Crown Castle asserts it is “enhancing,
densifying, expanding, or introducing new services.”° However, it has not established in any
factual manner what this means for the customer in terms of their “enhanced” experience.
Verizon customers in the surrounding areas of San Mateo Park are able to browse the internet,
watch films, video chat, use apps, send emails and do other high-speed data processes on mobile

devices. Very frequently, 5G is functionally indistinguishable from 4G LTE.*’ Providing service

The Ninth Circuit has questioned whether Section 332’s “anti-prohibition language even
covers situations, like that presented here, in which a telecommunications service provider seeks
to replace existing WCFs, as contrasted with the more typical situation in which the provider

seeks to construct new WCFs.”??

2. Gap in 5G Coverage Alone Cannot Amount to an Effective Prohibition of Personal

Wireless Services

Because cities traditionally have sole constitutional authority over local zoning decisions,
federal law only sought to preempt these decisions as necessary to ensure a functional
nationwide call network. The TCA does not give businesses the power to force cities to sweep
aside local design standards for the convenience of selling whatever forms of wireless product

they desire. The TCA only overrides local rules that prohibit “personal wireless services.”

This is defined to be “commercial mobile services, unlicensed wireless services, and
common carrier wireless exchange access services[,]” which are all forms of
“telecommunications services.”*° The TCA recognized two distinct types of service: one for
“information services,” which involve “a capability for generating, acquiring, storing,

transforming, processing, retrieving, utilizing, or making available information,”*! and that is

38 https://www.verizon.com/coverage-map/.
39 Id. at 727.

“047 U.S.C. § § 332(c)(7)(C).
41 Id. § 153(20).

809 of 846


--- page 810 ---
largely unregulated at the federal level, and another for “telecommunication” services, which are
“transmission[s], between or among points specified by the user, of information of the user’s
choosing, without change in the form or content[.]’”’? For instance, a traditional telephone call is
a telecommunication service because the carrier does not store, change or process the call but

rather only makes the connection in real-time before the callers.?

However, because Congress did not amend Section 332, the FCC continued to
acknowledged that not all forms of wireless transmissions qualify as “personal wireless services”
under Section 332.“4 Several federal district court decisions in the Second Circuit held that 4G
and 5G are a form of “information service” and gaps in mobile broadband coverage are not an
effective prohibition of personal wireless service.*> This issue has not been addressed by our
circuit and the Ninth Circuit has never overruled its existing two-prong “significant gap”

framework under Section 332 that focused on voice call coverage.*®

In Ohio Telecom Association v. FCC, on January 2, 2025, the Sixth Circuit, refused to
give deference to the FCC and struck down a Biden administration FCC order that redefined
mobile broadband, also known as 4G LTE and SG, as “telecommunications services” to give the
FCC more authority to impose net neutrality rule. The court held mobile broadband is an
“information service.”*” As a result, it “is not a commercial mobile service, it necessarily is a

private mobile service.”** This decision is binding on the FCC nationwide.

“3 In re Petitions for Declaratory Ruling on Regulatory Status of Wireless Messaging Serv. 33 FCC Red 12075,
12076 (Dec. 13, 2018) (FCC decreed that email, SMS and MMS are not “telecommunication services” because the
form of the transmission must be changed and stored by the provider rather than directly delivered between users.).
4 See, e.g., 47 C.F.R. § 1.6002(i) (discussing comingled services).

“ See, e.g., Crown Castle NG East LLC v. Town of Hempstead, 2018 WL 6605857, at *9 (E.D.N.Y. Dec. 17, 2018)
(“A gap in 4G coverage does not establish that the target area is underserved by voice cellular telephone service.”);
Extenet Sys., Inc. v. Vill. of Flower Hill, 617 F. Supp. 3d 125, 131 (E.D.N.Y. 2022) (“the stated intent of Verizon's
contract with ExteNet was to improve Verizon’s 4G LTE service. Indeed, it is undisputed that a signal strength far
less than Verizon's desired -85 dBm would still be sufficient to make a phone call. . . Improved capacity and speed
are desirable (and, no doubt, profitable) goals in the age of smartphones, but they are not protected by the Act.”).
“© Portland v. FCC, 969 F.3d 1020, 1034-35 (9th Cir. 2020) discuss a lower standard for a different section of the
TCA, Section 253, but not Section 332. In 2021, a federal court for our district held in New Singular Wireless PCS,
LLC v. County of Marin (N.D. Cal. Feb. 19, 2021, Case No. 20-cv-07915-SI) that Section 253 does not apply to
individualized determinations and applicants may not “challenge the denial of a zoning application under Section
253[.)”

https://www.opn.ca6.uscourts.gov/opinions.pdf/25a0002p-06.pdf.

810 of 846


--- page 811 ---
Crown Castle asserts that its 5G facility “would provide commercial mobile services and
qualifies as a personal wireless service facility.”*? While 28GHz antennas could potentially
provide both voice and data services, Crown Castle’s emphasis on “introducing the 5G

spectrum,”°°

a trade name for high-speed mobile broadband internet, showcases Crown Castle’s
goal is to offer that service. It makes no valid, evidentiary claim about providing any
telecommunication services. Ohio Telecom Association directly held that mobile broadband does

not qualify as “commercial mobile services” and is a “private mobile service.”>!

The express language of Section 332 declares that “private mobile service” is not a form
of “personal wireless services.”*? The Ninth Circuit recently confirmed that the TCA does not
preempt local regulation of “either information services or private mobile services.”*? As a
result, regardless of the level of existing mobile broadband coverage, the facility as described
cannot qualify for a variance since rejection will not result in an “effective denial of personal

wireless services” as interpreted by Ninth Circuit precedent.
Conclusion

As detailed in the appeal and this letter, Crown Castle’s application is fundamentally
flawed and does not meet the requirements of the City Policy or Wireless Ordinance and must be
denied. I look forward to having the opportunity to answering any questions from the

Commission at the hearing.

Draft Findings for Resolution Uphold Appeal of Wireless Permit for 401 Dorchester

(Permit# WC-2024-000246)

Based on the information set forth in the staff report, materials submitted by the parties to this
appeal, comments from the public, the hearing of March 12, 2025, and the public record as a
whole, be it resolved that the Commission finds that:

iL.

The Application is not in compliance with 2021 Design Standard #1 because the
Applicant has not demonstrated that it has minimized the height of the replacement pole.
The Application is not in compliance with 2021 Design Standard #2 because the
Applicant has not demonstrated that it has, to the maximum extent feasible, avoided
obstructing views from habitable areas, including the adjacent patio, such as by means of
reduced height replacement pole or use of alternative locations.

The Applicant has not established that it is eligible for an exception pursuant to SMMC
Chapter 17.10 and the 2021 Design Standards because

a)

b)

c)

d)

e)

The Applicant has not provided the Director with a reasonable and clearly defined

technical service objective based on factual information about the level of existing

coverage, extent of improvement in coverage or area of improved service.

The Applicant has not provided the Director with a meaningful comparative

analysis with the factual reasons why all alternative locations identified in the

Application are not technically feasible or available because it has excluded all

alternatives beyond 200 feet without factual justification based on the service

objective and capabilities of the proposed facility in the specific setting.

The Applicant has not provided the Director with a meaningful comparative

analysis with the factual reasons why all alternative locations identified in the

Application are not technically feasible or available because it has not explained

why Alternative 5 is unavailable based on GO-95 requirements, including by

means of a replacement pole.

The Applicant has not established that the proposed location is the least intrusive

as compared with the alternatives identified in the Application.

The Applicant has not established that an exception is necessary to avoid an

effective prohibition of provision of the Applicant’s personal wireless services

because

i. The Applicant has not provided facts showing that the 5G service it seeks
to provide qualifies as personal wireless services.
ii. The Applicant has not provided facts showing any significant gap in
personal wireless services.
